  • Oligomerization via the N-terminus of DnaA is also required for the initiation reaction .6 Initiation of replication occurs once per cell cycle and , during rapid growth , at all origins in the cell simultaneously .7 DnaA binding to the low-affinity sites , as well as binding of architectural elements ( Fis , IHF , and HU ) , may possibly contribute to the synchrony of initiation .8 -- 10 Two main mechanisms prevent initiation from reoccurring at already replicated origins and involve either inactivation of the newly replicated origin ( by sequestration ) or inactivation of the DnaA protein ( by hydrolysis of ATP-DnaA to ADP-DnaA ) .11,12 Specific inactivation of new origins occurs because new origins are hemimethylated ( i.e. , adenine nucleotides of GATC sites are methylated on only one strand ) .13,14 The SeqA protein binds to the hemimethylated GATC sites and prevents remethylation by Dam methylase .15 Regions on the chromosome that have high numbers of GATC sites ( oriC and dnaA promoter ) remain hemimethylated considerably longer ( for up to one-third of a cell cycle ) than regions with few GATC sites .14,16 Also a region with an artificially high number of GATC sites ( an oriC-like distribution of GATC sites placed in the tnaA gene ) was found to be sequestered as long as oriC , showing that sequestration depends on the concentration and distribution of GATC sites .17 During sequestration of newly replicated origins , ATP-DnaA is hydrolyzed to ADP-DnaA in a process that requires the Hda protein and the DNA-loaded β-clamp subunit of the DNA polymerase III holoenzyme .18 This process contributes to lowering the initiation potential by lowering the proportion of ATP-form DnaA .19 The total amount of free DnaA is also lowered because new DnaA binding sites are generated by replication .20,21 After sequestration , the initiation potential is low , and initiation does not occur until a generation has passed . [18835566]
  • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative-stress .6,11 -14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown . [20936830]

[8973312]

  • We show that the activity of the ilvPG promoter increases with increased negative supercoiling and that this sensitivity to superhelical density is enhanced in the presence of IHF . [8702758]
  • These conclusions are based on the in vitro observations that : ( i ) although promoter activity is increased by DNA supercoiling , both in the presence and absence of IHF the relative activity of the promoter remains the same over a wide range of template DNA superhelical densities ( Fig. 5 ) ; and ( ii ) IHF binds with indistinguishable affinities to relaxed and supercoiled DNA templates ( Fig. 9 ; Ref . [8702758]
  • These data suggest that IHF does not affect the overall response of the ilvPG promoter to changes in superhelical DNA density ; rather , in the presence of IHF , promoter activity is more sensitive to small changes in the superhelical density of the DNA template in the physiological range of s 5 20.03 to 20.09 . [8702758]
  • In the absence of IHF , promoter activity increases with increased DNA supercoiling . [8702758]
  • That is , the superhelical DNA density that produced half-maximal promoter activity in the presence of IHF was the same as the superhelical DNA density that produced half-maximal promoter activity in the absence of IHF ( Figs. 4 and 5 ) . [8702758]
  • In the presence of IHF , the same increases in superhelical DNA densities result in larger increases in promoter activity until a maximal activation of 5-fold is obtained . [8702758]
  • However , in the presence of IHF , increases in superhelical DNA densities resulted in larger increases in promoter activity until a maximal activation of 5-fold was obtained at a superhelical DNA density of s 5 20.09 ( Figs. 4 and 6 ) . [8702758]
  • IHF also activates transcription from this promoter by increasing the rate of the isomerization step and , in the presence of IHF , the activating effect of increased negative DNA supercoiling is enhanced . [8702758]
  • Thus , although both increased DNA supercoiling and IHF facilitate the unwinding of the DNA helix and the rate of promoter open complex formation ( 7 ) , our results suggest that the activation of this rate-limiting step in the transcription initiation reaction by DNA supercoiling and IHF are effected by distinctly different mechanisms .   • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative stress.6,11-14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown . [20936830]

  • Hha partially represses biofilm-formation through type I fimbriation via fimA and ihfA Along with fimA , the main structural component of type I fimbriae , hha deletion induced ihfA ; ihfA is a subunit of the IHF global regulator that is required for the normal expression of fimA , as mutations in ihfA or in the IHF beta-subunit ihfB ( also induced upon hha deletion ) prevent the phase variation expression of fimA [ 11 ] .   • Other lines of evidence found here linking Hha to fimbriae include ( ii ) ihfA encoding a subunit of the IHF regulator that is an activator of type I fimbriae production via the fimA promoter [ 11 ] is activated in all the LB glu microarrays upon hha deletion ( Table S1 ) , ( iii ) Hha represses fimA and ihfA transcription in biofilm cells as shown by RT-PCR , ( iv ) fimA and ihfA mutations abolish biofilm-formation , ( v ) deleting hha along with either fimA and ihfA ( double mutants ) fails to increase biofilm-formation , ( vi ) transcription of fimA and ihfA is induced in the hha deletion mutant and is inhibited by overexpressing hha ( GFP reporter constructs ) ( Figure 4 ) , and ( vii ) type I fimbriae production dramatically increases in the absence of hha and Hha overexpression inhibits type I fimbriation ( Figure 3 ) .   • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor-biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA-metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative stress.6,11-14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown .   • IHF belongs to a family of bacterial histone-like DNA binding proteins that facilitate the assembly of ordered protein-DNA structures by bringing distant DNA sequences , or proteins bound at distant DNA sites , into close proximity to one another ( for a review , see Schmid , 1990 ) . [1569580]
